     <p>
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Plot">
       Plot
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Spider-Man_(2002_film)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Plot">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <p>
      High school student
      <a href="/wiki/Spider-Man" title="Spider-Man">
       Peter Parker
      </a>
      visits a genetics laboratory with his best friend
      <a href="/wiki/Harry_Osborn" title="Harry Osborn">
       Harry Osborn
      </a>
      and Peter's love interest,
      <a href="/wiki/Mary_Jane_Watson" title="Mary Jane Watson">
       Mary Jane Watson
      </a>
      . There, Peter is bitten on the hand by a
      <a href="/wiki/Genetic_engineering" title="Genetic engineering">
       genetically engineered
      </a>
      "super spider". Shortly after arriving home to his
      <a href="/wiki/Aunt_May" title="Aunt May">
       Aunt May
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Uncle_Ben" title="Uncle Ben">
       Uncle Ben
      </a>
      , he is rendered unconscious. Meanwhile, Harry's father, scientist
      <a href="/wiki/Green_Goblin" title="Green Goblin">
       Norman Osborn
      </a>
      , owner of
      <a href="/wiki/Oscorp" title="Oscorp">
       Oscorp
      </a>
      , is attempting to preserve his company's critically important military contract. He experiments on himself with a new but unstable performance-enhancing chemical vapor that hugely increases his speed, strength, and stamina. However, it also drives him insane and he kills his assistant,
      <a href="/wiki/Mendel_Stromm" title="Mendel Stromm">
       Mendel Stromm
      </a>
      . The next morning, Peter finds that his previously impaired vision has improved and that his body has
      <a href="/wiki/Metamorphosis" title="Metamorphosis">
       metamorphosized
      </a>
      into a more muscular physique. At school, he finds his body producing webbing and that his quickened reflexes let him avoid injury during a confrontation with bully
      <a href="/wiki/Flash_Thompson" title="Flash Thompson">
       Flash Thompson
      </a>
      . Peter discovers he has developed superhuman speed, strength, the ability to stick to surfaces, and a heightened ability to sense danger.
     </p>
     <p>
      Brushing off Uncle Ben's advice that "With great power comes great responsibility," Peter enters a wrestling tournament to get money to buy a car and impress Mary Jane. He wins his match, but the promoter cheats him out of the contest money. When a
      <a href="/wiki/Burglar_(comics)" title="Burglar (comics)">
       thief
      </a>
      steals money from the promoter, Peter allows the thief to escape as revenge. He later discovers his Uncle Ben has been carjacked and shot dead. Peter chases down and confronts the carjacker in a warehouse only to realize it was the same thief he let get away. After Peter disarms him, the fleeing carjacker falls out a window to his death. Meanwhile, Norman Osborn kills several scientists and the military's General Slocum.
     </p>
     <p>
      Upon graduating from high school, Peter begins using his abilities to fight injustice, donning a costume and the persona of Spider-Man. Loudmouthed newspaper editor
      <a href="/wiki/J._Jonah_Jameson" title="J. Jonah Jameson">
       J. Jonah Jameson
      </a>
      hires him as a
      <a href="/wiki/Freelancer" title="Freelancer">
       freelance
      </a>
      <a href="/wiki/Photographer" title="Photographer">
       photographer
      </a>
      , since Peter is the only person providing clear images of Spider-Man.
     </p>
     <p>
      Norman, upon learning Oscorp's board members plan to sell the company, assassinates them at the World Unity Fair. Jameson quickly dubs the mysterious killer the
      <a href="/wiki/Green_Goblin" title="Green Goblin">
       Green Goblin
      </a>
      . The Goblin offers Spider-Man a place at his side, but Spider-Man refuses. At the Osborn and Parkers'
      <a href="/wiki/Thanksgiving_(United_States)" title="Thanksgiving (United States)">
       Thanksgiving
      </a>
      dinner, Norman, unknown to Peter, deduces Spider-Man's true identity; the Green Goblin subsequently attacks and hospitalizes Aunt May.
     </p>
     <p>
      Mary Jane admits she has a crush on Spider-Man, who has rescued her on numerous occasions, and she asks Peter whether Spider-Man ever asked about her. Harry, who loves Mary Jane, arrives and learns she does not feel likewise toward him. Devastated, Harry tells his father that Peter loves Mary Jane, unintentionally revealing Spider-Man's biggest weakness.
     </p>
     <p>
      The Goblin kidnaps and holds Mary Jane and a
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Roosevelt_Island_Tram" title="Roosevelt Island Tram">
       Roosevelt Island Tram
      </a>
      car full of children hostage alongside the
      <a href="/wiki/Queensboro_Bridge" title="Queensboro Bridge">
       Queensboro Bridge
      </a>
      . There, he forces Spider-Man to choose who he wants to save, and drops Mary Jane and the children. Spider-Man manages to save both Mary Jane and the tram car, while the Goblin is pelted by civilians on the bridge showing loyalty to Spider-Man and contempt for the Goblin's evil deeds. The Goblin then grabs Spider-Man and throws him into an abandoned building where they battle with the Goblin gaining the upper hand. When the Goblin boasts of how he will later subject Mary Jane to a slow and painful death, an enraged Spider-Man overpowers the Goblin, unmasking him.
     </p>
     <p>
      Norman begs for forgiveness, but his Goblin persona attempts to remote-control his glider to impale Spider-Man. The superhero avoids the attack, causing the glider to impale Norman instead, finally killing him. In his dying breath, Norman tells Peter not to reveal his crimes to Harry. Spider-Man takes Norman's body back to Osborn's house and hides the Green Goblin's equipment. At Norman’s funeral, Harry swears vengeance toward Spider-Man, believing him responsible for killing his father, and asserts that Peter is all he has left. Mary Jane confesses to Peter she is in love with him, but Peter, feeling that he must protect her from the unwanted attentions of Spider-Man's enemies, hides his true feelings and tells her that they can only be friends. As Peter leaves the funeral, he recalls Ben's words about responsibility, and accepts his new life as Spider-Man.
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Cast">
       Cast
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Spider-Man_(2002_film)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Cast">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <table cellspacing="5" class="toccolours" style="float: right; margin-left: 1em; margin-right: 2em; font-size: 85%; background:#c6dbf7; color:black; width:30em; max-width: 40%;">
      <tbody>
       <tr>
        <td style="text-align: left;">
         "I felt like I was an outsider. I think what happened to me made me develop this street sense of watching people and working out what made them tick, wondering whether I could trust them or not. I went to a lot of schools along the coast in California, made few friends and stayed with aunts, uncles and grandparents while my folks tried to make ends meet. It was tough. We had no money."
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <td style="text-align: left;">
         — Tobey Maguire on identifying with Peter Parker.
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-lonely_2-0">
          <a href="#cite_note-lonely-2">
           <span>
            [
           </span>
           2
           <span>
            ]
           </span>
          </a>
         </sup>
        </td>
       </tr>
      </tbody>
     </table>
     <ul>
      <li>
       <a href="/wiki/Tobey_Maguire" title="Tobey Maguire">
        Tobey Maguire
       </a>
       as
       <a href="/wiki/Spider-Man" title="Spider-Man">
        Peter Parker / Spider-Man
       </a>
       :
       <br/>
       Peter is an academically brilliant but socially inept boy who is bitten by a
       <a href="/wiki/Genetic_engineering" title="Genetic engineering">
        genetically modified
       </a>
       spider and gains spider-like abilities. Maguire was cast as Peter in July 2000,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-spins_3-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-spins-3">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         3
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
       having been
       <a href="/wiki/Sam_Raimi" title="Sam Raimi">
        Sam Raimi
       </a>
       's primary choice for the role after he saw
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/The_Cider_House_Rules_(film)" title="The Cider House Rules (film)">
         The Cider House Rules
        </a>
       </i>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-empire_4-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-empire-4">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         4
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
       The studio was initially hesitant to cast someone who did not seem to fit the ranks of "adrenaline-pumping, tail-kicking titans",
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-spins_3-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-spins-3">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         3
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
       but Maguire managed to impress studio executives with his audition. The actor was signed for a deal in the range of $3 to $4 million with higher salary options for two sequels.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-spins_3-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-spins-3">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         3
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
       To prepare, Maguire was trained by a physical trainer, a yoga instructor, a martial arts expert, and a climbing expert, taking several months to improve his physique.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-friday_5-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-friday-5">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         5
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
       Maguire studied spiders and worked with a wire man to simulate the arachnidlike motion, and had a special diet.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6">
        <a href="#cite_note-6">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         6
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
      </li>
     </ul>
     <dl>
      <dd>
       The studio had expressed interest in actors
       <a href="/wiki/Leonardo_DiCaprio" title="Leonardo DiCaprio">
        Leonardo DiCaprio
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Edward_Furlong" title="Edward Furlong">
        Edward Furlong
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Freddie_Prinze,_Jr." title="Freddie Prinze, Jr.">
        Freddie Prinze, Jr
       </a>
       ,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-unraveling_7-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-unraveling-7">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         7
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
       <a href="/wiki/Chris_Klein_(actor)" title="Chris Klein (actor)">
        Chris Klein
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Wes_Bentley" title="Wes Bentley">
        Wes Bentley
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Heath_Ledger" title="Heath Ledger">
        Heath Ledger
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hughes_8-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-hughes-8">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         8
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
       <a href="/wiki/Edward_Furlong" title="Edward Furlong">
        Edward Furlong
       </a>
       had been considered by
       <a href="/wiki/James_Cameron" title="James Cameron">
        James Cameron
       </a>
       for the role in 1996,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9">
        <a href="#cite_note-9">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         9
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
       while Raimi joked of Prinze that "[he] won't even be allowed to buy a ticket to see this film."
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hughes_8-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-hughes-8">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         8
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
       In addition, actors
       <a href="/wiki/Scott_Speedman" title="Scott Speedman">
        Scott Speedman
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Jay_Rodan" title="Jay Rodan">
        Jay Rodan
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/James_Franco" title="James Franco">
        James Franco
       </a>
       were involved in screen tests for the lead role.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10">
        <a href="#cite_note-10">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         10
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
      </dd>
     </dl>
     <ul>
      <li>
       <a href="/wiki/Willem_Dafoe" title="Willem Dafoe">
        Willem Dafoe
       </a>
       as
       <a href="/wiki/Norman_Osborn" title="Norman Osborn">
        Norman Osborn
       </a>
       /
       <a href="/wiki/Green_Goblin" title="Green Goblin">
        Green Goblin
       </a>
       :
       <br/>
       CEO of Oscorp who tests an unstable strength enhancer on himself and becomes the insane and powerful Green Goblin. Unaware of Spider-Man's true identity, he also sees himself as a father figure for Peter, ignoring his own son, Harry. Dafoe was cast as Osborn in November 2000,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11">
        <a href="#cite_note-11">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         11
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
       after
       <a href="/wiki/Nicolas_Cage" title="Nicolas Cage">
        Nicolas Cage
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/John_Malkovich" title="John Malkovich">
        John Malkovich
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/John_Travolta" title="John Travolta">
        John Travolta
       </a>
       turned down the role.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12">
        <a href="#cite_note-12">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         12
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13">
        <a href="#cite_note-13">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         13
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
       Dafoe insisted on wearing the uncomfortable costume as he felt that a stuntman would not convey the character's necessary body language. The 580-piece suit took half an hour to put on.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hughes_8-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-hughes-8">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         8
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
      </li>
      <li>
       <a href="/wiki/Kirsten_Dunst" title="Kirsten Dunst">
        Kirsten Dunst
       </a>
       as
       <a href="/wiki/Mary_Jane_Watson" title="Mary Jane Watson">
        Mary Jane Watson
       </a>
       :
       <br/>
       The girl whom Peter Parker has developed a crush since he was six years old. Mary Jane has an abusive father, and aspires to become an actress, but becomes a waitress at a run down diner, a fact she hides from her boyfriend, Harry. Before Raimi cast Dunst, he had expressed his interest in casting
       <a href="/wiki/Alicia_Witt" title="Alicia Witt">
        Alicia Witt
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14">
        <a href="#cite_note-14">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         14
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
       Dunst decided to audition after learning Maguire had been cast, feeling the film would have a more independent feel.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15">
        <a href="#cite_note-15">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         15
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
       Dunst earned the role a month before shooting in an audition in
       <a href="/wiki/Berlin" title="Berlin">
        Berlin
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hughes_8-3">
        <a href="#cite_note-hughes-8">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         8
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
      </li>
      <li>
       <a href="/wiki/James_Franco" title="James Franco">
        James Franco
       </a>
       as
       <a href="/wiki/Harry_Osborn" title="Harry Osborn">
        Harry Osborn
       </a>
       :
       <br/>
       Before being cast as Peter's best friend and flatmate, Franco had screen tested for Spider-Man himself.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16">
        <a href="#cite_note-16">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         16
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
      </li>
      <li>
       <a href="/wiki/Cliff_Robertson" title="Cliff Robertson">
        Cliff Robertson
       </a>
       as
       <a href="/wiki/Uncle_Ben" title="Uncle Ben">
        Ben Parker
       </a>
       :
       <br/>
       May Parker's husband and Peter Parker's uncle, a fired
       <a href="/wiki/Electrician" title="Electrician">
        electrician
       </a>
       who is trying to find a new job. He is killed by a carjacker whom Peter failed to stop, and leaves Peter with the message, "With great power comes great responsibility."
      </li>
      <li>
       <a href="/wiki/Rosemary_Harris" title="Rosemary Harris">
        Rosemary Harris
       </a>
       as
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/May_Parker" title="May Parker">
        May Parker
       </a>
       :
       <br/>
       Ben Parker's wife and Peter Parker's aunt who is highly aware of Peter's love for Mary Jane.
      </li>
      <li>
       <a href="/wiki/J._K._Simmons" title="J. K. Simmons">
        J. K. Simmons
       </a>
       as
       <a href="/wiki/J._Jonah_Jameson" title="J. Jonah Jameson">
        J. Jonah Jameson
       </a>
       :
       <br/>
       The grouchy publisher of the
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Daily_Bugle" title="Daily Bugle">
         Daily Bugle
        </a>
       </i>
       who despises Spider-Man. Nonetheless, he has a good side and pays Peter for photos of Spider-Man, and refuses to tell the Green Goblin the identity of the photographer.
      </li>
      <li>
       <a href="/wiki/Joe_Manganiello" title="Joe Manganiello">
        Joe Manganiello
       </a>
       as
       <a href="/wiki/Flash_Thompson" title="Flash Thompson">
        Eugene "Flash" Thompson
       </a>
       :
       <br/>
       A repugnant high school bully who bullies Peter, and is defeated in a fight after Peter inherits his spider powers.
      </li>
      <li>
       <a href="/wiki/Bill_Nunn" title="Bill Nunn">
        Bill Nunn
       </a>
       as
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Joseph_%22Robbie%22_Robertson" title='Joseph "Robbie" Robertson'>
        Joseph "Robbie" Robertson
       </a>
       :
       <br/>
       The kindly editor at the
       <i>
        Daily Bugle
       </i>
       , who on occasion helps Peter.
      </li>
      <li>
       <a href="/wiki/Michael_Papajohn" title="Michael Papajohn">
        Michael Papajohn
       </a>
       as
       <a href="/wiki/Burglar_(comics)" title="Burglar (comics)">
        the Carjacker
       </a>
       :
       <br/>
       The criminal who robs the wrestling manager who refuses to pay Peter Parker for his ring performance and later murders Ben Parker when he carjacks him in the course of his escape. He is killed from falling from a window when confronted by Peter.
      </li>
      <li>
       <a href="/wiki/Elizabeth_Banks" title="Elizabeth Banks">
        Elizabeth Banks
       </a>
       as
       <a href="/wiki/Betty_Brant" title="Betty Brant">
        Betty Brant
       </a>
       :
       <br/>
       As seen in past
       <i>
        Spider-Man
       </i>
       comics, Betty Brant is Jameson's secretary who has a bit of a soft spot for Peter.
      </li>
     </ul>
     <p>
      <a href="/wiki/Bruce_Campbell" title="Bruce Campbell">
       Bruce Campbell
      </a>
      , a long-time colleague of director
      <a href="/wiki/Sam_Raimi" title="Sam Raimi">
       Sam Raimi
      </a>
      , has a cameo as the announcer at the wrestling ring Peter takes part in.
      <a href="/wiki/Ted_Raimi" title="Ted Raimi">
       Ted Raimi
      </a>
      , Sam Raimi's actor brother, plays a small role as editor's assistant "Hoffman". Sam Raimi himself appeared off-screen, throwing
      <a href="/wiki/Popcorn" title="Popcorn">
       popcorn
      </a>
      at Peter as he enters the arena to wrestle Bonesaw McGraw (played by former professional wrestler
      <a href="/wiki/Randy_Savage" title="Randy Savage">
       "Macho Man" Randy Savage
      </a>
      ).
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-producer_commentary_17-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-producer_commentary-17">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        17
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <i>
       Spider-Man
      </i>
      co-creator
      <a href="/wiki/Stan_Lee" title="Stan Lee">
       Stan Lee
      </a>
      also has a cameo, in which he asks Peter, "Hey kid, would you like a pair of these glasses? They're the kind they wore in
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/X-Men_(film)" title="X-Men (film)">
        X-Men
       </a>
      </i>
      ." The scene was cut, and Lee only briefly appears in the film to grab a young girl from falling debris during the battle between Spider-Man and the Green Goblin in
      <a href="/wiki/Times_Square" title="Times Square">
       Times Square
      </a>
      .
      <a href="/wiki/Rhythm_and_blues" title="Rhythm and blues">
       R&amp;B
      </a>
      /
      <a href="/wiki/Soul_music" title="Soul music">
       soul
      </a>
      singer
      <a href="/wiki/Macy_Gray" title="Macy Gray">
       Macy Gray
      </a>
      appears as herself.
      <a href="/wiki/Lucy_Lawless" title="Lucy Lawless">
       Lucy Lawless
      </a>
      , star of
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Xena:_Warrior_Princess" title="Xena: Warrior Princess">
        Xena: Warrior Princess
       </a>
      </i>
      (produced by Raimi), also appears as a punk rock girl. One of the stunt performers in the film is actor
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Johnny_Tri_Nguyen" title="Johnny Tri Nguyen">
       Johnny Tri Nguyen
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-empire_4-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-empire-4">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        4
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <a href="/wiki/Octavia_Spencer" title="Octavia Spencer">
       Octavia Spencer
      </a>
      has a brief appearance as the check-in girl who signs Peter Parker into the wrestling match and warns him that they are not liable for the injuries he will sustain.
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Production">
       Production
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Spider-Man_(2002_film)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Production">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Development">
       Development
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Spider-Man_(2002_film)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Development">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="hatnote boilerplate seealso">
      For more details on this topic, see
      <a href="/wiki/Spider-Man_in_film#Development" title="Spider-Man in film">
       Spider-Man in film § Development
      </a>
      .
     </div>
     <p>
      In April 1999, although
      <a href="/wiki/Sony_Pictures_Entertainment" title="Sony Pictures Entertainment">
       Sony Pictures
      </a>
      optioned from
      <a href="/wiki/Metro-Goldwyn-Mayer" title="Metro-Goldwyn-Mayer">
       Metro-Goldwyn-Mayer
      </a>
      all preceding script versions of
      <i>
       Spider-Man
      </i>
      , it only exercised the options on "the Cameron material," which contractually included a multi-author screenplay and a forty-five page "
      <a href="/wiki/Scriptment" title="Scriptment">
       scriptment
      </a>
      " credited only to
      <a href="/wiki/James_Cameron" title="James Cameron">
       James Cameron
      </a>
      . The studio announced they were not hiring Cameron himself to direct the film.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18">
       <a href="#cite_note-18">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        18
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The studio lined up
      <a href="/wiki/Roland_Emmerich" title="Roland Emmerich">
       Roland Emmerich
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Tim_Burton" title="Tim Burton">
       Tim Burton
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Chris_Columbus_(filmmaker)" title="Chris Columbus (filmmaker)">
       Chris Columbus
      </a>
      , and
      <a href="/wiki/David_Fincher" title="David Fincher">
       David Fincher
      </a>
      as potential directors. Fincher did not want to depict the
      <a href="/wiki/Origin_story" title="Origin story">
       origin story
      </a>
      , pitching the film as being based on
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/The_Night_Gwen_Stacy_Died" title="The Night Gwen Stacy Died">
        The Night Gwen Stacy Died
       </a>
      </i>
      storyline, but the studio disagreed.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hughes_8-4">
       <a href="#cite_note-hughes-8">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        8
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <a href="/wiki/Sam_Raimi" title="Sam Raimi">
       Sam Raimi
      </a>
      was attached to direct in January 2000,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ahead_19-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-ahead-19">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        19
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      for a summer 2001 release.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20">
       <a href="#cite_note-20">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        20
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      He had been a big fan of the comic book during his youth, and his passion for
      <i>
       Spider-Man
      </i>
      earned him the job.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HBO_21-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-HBO-21">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        21
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Cameron's work became the basis of
      <a href="/wiki/David_Koepp" title="David Koepp">
       David Koepp
      </a>
      's first draft screenplay, often word for word.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hiltzik_22-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Hiltzik-22">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        22
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Cameron's versions of the Marvel villains Electro and Sandman remained the antagonists. Koepp's rewrite substituted the
      <a href="/wiki/Green_Goblin" title="Green Goblin">
       Green Goblin
      </a>
      as the main antagonist and added
      <a href="/wiki/Doctor_Octopus" title="Doctor Octopus">
       Doctor Octopus
      </a>
      as the secondary antagonist.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23">
       <a href="#cite_note-23">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        23
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Raimi felt the Green Goblin and the surrogate father-son theme between Norman Osborn and Peter Parker would be more interesting.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-trivia_track_24-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-trivia_track-24">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        24
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      In June, Columbia hired
      <a href="/wiki/Scott_Rosenberg" title="Scott Rosenberg">
       Scott Rosenberg
      </a>
      to rewrite Koepp's material. Remaining a constant in all the rewrites was the "organic webshooter" idea from the Cameron "scriptment".
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25">
       <a href="#cite_note-25">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        25
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Raimi felt he would stretch the audience's
      <a href="/wiki/Suspension_of_disbelief" title="Suspension of disbelief">
       suspension of disbelief
      </a>
      too far to have Peter invent mechanical webshooters.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-friday_5-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-friday-5">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        5
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Rosenberg removed Doctor Octopus and created several new action sequences.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26">
       <a href="#cite_note-26">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        26
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Raimi felt adding a third origin story would make the film too complex. Sequences removed from the final film had Spider-Man protecting Fargas, the wheelchair-using Oscorp executive from the Goblin, and Spider-Man defusing a hostage situation on a train.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hughes_8-5">
       <a href="#cite_note-hughes-8">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        8
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      As production neared, producer
      <a href="/wiki/Laura_Ziskin" title="Laura Ziskin">
       Laura Ziskin
      </a>
      hired her husband, award-winning writer
      <a href="/wiki/Alvin_Sargent" title="Alvin Sargent">
       Alvin Sargent
      </a>
      , to polish the dialogue, primarily between Peter and Mary Jane.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-greg_27-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-greg-27">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        27
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Columbia offered David Koepp's name to the
      <a href="/wiki/Writers_Guild_of_America" title="Writers Guild of America">
       WGA
      </a>
      as sole screenwriter, despite the fact that it had acquired Cameron's script and hired two subsequent writers. Without reading and comparing any of the material, the Writers Guild approved sole credit to Koepp.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hiltzik_22-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-Hiltzik-22">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        22
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Filming">
       Filming
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Spider-Man_(2002_film)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Filming">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      With
      <i>
       Spider-Man
      </i>
      cast, filming was set to begin the following November in
      <a href="/wiki/New_York_City" title="New York City">
       New York City
      </a>
      and on Sony
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Soundstage" title="Soundstage">
       soundstages
      </a>
      . The film was set for release a year later,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-spins_3-3">
       <a href="#cite_note-spins-3">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        3
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      but when the film was postponed to be released on May 3, 2002,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28">
       <a href="#cite_note-28">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        28
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      filming officially began on January 8, 2001
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-greg_27-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-greg-27">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        27
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      in
      <a href="/wiki/Culver_City,_California" title="Culver City, California">
       Culver City, California
      </a>
      . After the
      <a href="/wiki/September_11_attacks" title="September 11 attacks">
       terrorist attacks on September 11, 2001
      </a>
      , certain sequences were re-filmed, and images of the
      <a href="/wiki/World_Trade_Center" title="World Trade Center">
       Twin Towers
      </a>
      were digitally erased from the film.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29">
       <a href="#cite_note-29">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        29
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30">
       <a href="#cite_note-30">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        30
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Sony's Stage 29 was used for Peter's
      <a href="/wiki/Forest_Hills,_Queens" title="Forest Hills, Queens">
       Forest Hills
      </a>
      home, and Stage 27 was used for the wrestling sequence where Peter takes on Bonesaw McGraw (
      <a href="/wiki/Randy_Savage" title="Randy Savage">
       Randy Savage
      </a>
      ). Stage 27 was also used for the complex
      <a href="/wiki/Times_Square" title="Times Square">
       Times Square
      </a>
      sequence where Spider-Man and the Goblin battle for the first time, where a three-story set with a breakaway balcony piece was built. The scene also required shooting in
      <a href="/wiki/Downey,_California" title="Downey, California">
       Downey, California
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-booklet_31-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-booklet-31">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        31
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      On March 6,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32">
       <a href="#cite_note-32">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        32
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      forty-five-year-old construction worker Tim Holcombe was killed when a forklift modified as a construction crane crashed into a construction basket that he was in. The following court case led to the California Division of Occupational Safety and Health to fine Sony $58,805.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33">
       <a href="#cite_note-33">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        33
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      In
      <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles" title="Los Angeles">
       Los Angeles
      </a>
      , locations included the
      <a href="/wiki/Natural_History_Museum_of_Los_Angeles_County" title="Natural History Museum of Los Angeles County">
       Natural History Museum
      </a>
      (for the
      <a href="/wiki/Columbia_University" title="Columbia University">
       Columbia University
      </a>
      lab where Peter is bitten and receives his powers), the Pacific Electricity Building (the
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Daily_Bugle" title="Daily Bugle">
        Daily Bugle
       </a>
      </i>
      offices) and
      <a href="/wiki/Greystone_Mansion" title="Greystone Mansion">
       Greystone Mansion
      </a>
      (for the interiors of Norman Osborn's home). In April, 4 of the Spider-Man costumes were stolen, and Sony put up a $25,000 reward for their return.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34">
       <a href="#cite_note-34">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        34
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      They were recovered after 18 months and a former movie studio security guard and an accomplice were arrested.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35">
       <a href="#cite_note-35">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        35
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Production moved to New York City for two weeks, taking in locations such as the
      <a href="/wiki/Queensboro_Bridge" title="Queensboro Bridge">
       Queensboro Bridge
      </a>
      , the exteriors of Columbia University's
      <a href="/wiki/Low_Memorial_Library" title="Low Memorial Library">
       Low Memorial Library
      </a>
      and the
      <a href="/wiki/New_York_Public_Library" title="New York Public Library">
       New York Public Library
      </a>
      , and a rooftop garden in the
      <a href="/wiki/Rockefeller_Center" title="Rockefeller Center">
       Rockefeller Center
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-booklet_31-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-booklet-31">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        31
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The crew returned to Los Angeles where production and filming ended in June. The
      <a href="/wiki/Flatiron_Building" title="Flatiron Building">
       Flatiron Building
      </a>
      was used for the
      <i>
       Daily Bugle
      </i>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-greg_27-2">
       <a href="#cite_note-greg-27">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        27
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Design">
       Design
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Spider-Man_(2002_film)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Design">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      Although it wound up being faithful to the comics, many designs were made for Spider-Man's costumes: one concept costume designer
      <a href="/wiki/James_Acheson" title="James Acheson">
       James Acheson
      </a>
      became fond of had a red emblem over a black costume.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hughes_8-6">
       <a href="#cite_note-hughes-8">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        8
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      To create Spider-Man's costume, Maguire was fitted for the skintight suit, being covered with layers of substance to create the suit's shape.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36">
       <a href="#cite_note-36">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        36
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      It was designed as a single piece, except for the mask. The webbing, which accented the costume, was cut by computer. The mask eye lenses were designed to have a mirror look.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37">
       <a href="#cite_note-37">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        37
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Effects">
       Effects
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Spider-Man_(2002_film)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Effects">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      Visual effects supervisor
      <a href="/wiki/John_Dykstra" title="John Dykstra">
       John Dykstra
      </a>
      was hired to produce the film's visual effects in May 2000.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38">
       <a href="#cite_note-38">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        38
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      He convinced Raimi to make many of the stunts
      <a href="/wiki/Computer-generated_imagery" title="Computer-generated imagery">
       computer generated
      </a>
      , as they would have been physically impossible. Raimi had used more traditional special effects in his previous films and learned a lot about using computers during production.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HBO_21-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-HBO-21">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        21
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Raimi worked hard to plan all the sequences of Spider-Man swinging from buildings, which he described as, "
      <a href="/wiki/Ballet" title="Ballet">
       ballet
      </a>
      in the sky." The complexity of such sequences meant the budget rose from an initially planned $70 million to around $100 million.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-empire_4-2">
       <a href="#cite_note-empire-4">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        4
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Shots were made more complicated because of the main characters' individual color schemes, so Spider-Man and the Green Goblin had to be shot separately for effects shots: Spider-Man was shot in front of a
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Greenscreen" title="Greenscreen">
       greenscreen
      </a>
      , while the Green Goblin was shot against bluescreen. Shooting them together would have resulted in one character being erased from a shot.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hughes_8-7">
       <a href="#cite_note-hughes-8">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        8
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Saki said the biggest difficulty of creating Spider-Man was that as the character was masked, it immediately lost a lot of characterization. Without the context of eyes or mouth, a lot of body language had to be put in so that there would be emotional content. Raimi wanted to convey the essence of Spider-Man as being, "the transition that occurs between him being a young man going through puberty and being a superhero." Dykstra said his crew of animators had never reached such a level of sophistication to give subtle hints of still making Spider-Man feel like a human being.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39">
       <a href="#cite_note-39">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        39
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      When two studio executives were shown shots of the computer generated character, they believed it was actually Maguire performing stunts.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hughes_8-8">
       <a href="#cite_note-hughes-8">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        8
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      In addition, Dykstra's crew had to composite areas of New York City and replaced every car in shots with digital models. Raimi did not want it to feel entirely like animation, so none of the shots were 100% computer generated.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40">
       <a href="#cite_note-40">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        40
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Release">
       Release
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Spider-Man_(2002_film)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Release">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Bannedposter.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="332" data-file-width="225" height="295" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/2/24/Bannedposter.jpg/200px-Bannedposter.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/2/24/Bannedposter.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/2/24/Bannedposter.jpg 2x" width="200"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Bannedposter.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        Original
        <i>
         Spider-Man
        </i>
        teaser poster, which was recalled from theatres following
        <a href="/wiki/September_11_attacks" title="September 11 attacks">
         9/11
        </a>
        (the
        <a href="/wiki/World_Trade_Center" title="World Trade Center">
         World Trade Center
        </a>
        is reflected in Spider-Man's eyes)
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      After the
      <a href="/wiki/September_11_attacks" title="September 11 attacks">
       terrorist attacks
      </a>
      on the United States on September 11, 2001, Sony recalled teaser posters which showed a close-up of Spider-Man's face with the New York skyline (including, prominently, the
      <a href="/wiki/World_Trade_Center" title="World Trade Center">
       World Trade Center
      </a>
      towers) reflected in his eyes. The film's original
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Teaser_trailer" title="Teaser trailer">
       teaser trailer
      </a>
      , released in 2001 and shown before
      <a href="/wiki/Jurassic_Park_III" title="Jurassic Park III">
       Jurassic Park III
      </a>
      , featured a mini-film plot involving a group of bank robbers escaping in a
      <a href="/wiki/Eurocopter_AS355" title="Eurocopter AS355">
       Eurocopter AS355 Twin Squirrel
      </a>
      helicopter, which gets caught from behind and propelled backward into what at first appears to be a net, then is shown to be a gigantic spider web spun between the
      <a href="/wiki/World_Trade_Center" title="World Trade Center">
       World Trade Center's
      </a>
      towers. According to Sony, the trailer did not contain any actual footage from the film itself and is consequently one of the most popular "Special Shoot" trailers since
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Terminator_2:_Judgment_Day" title="Terminator 2: Judgment Day">
        Terminator 2: Judgment Day
       </a>
      </i>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41">
       <a href="#cite_note-41">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        41
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The trailer and poster were pulled after the events of the September 11, 2001 attacks, but can be found on the Internet on websites such as YouTube.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42">
       <a href="#cite_note-42">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        42
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Before the film's
      <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">
       British
      </a>
      theatrical release in June 2002, the
      <a href="/wiki/British_Board_of_Film_Classification" title="British Board of Film Classification">
       British Board of Film Classification
      </a>
      (BBFC) gave the film a '12' certificate. Due to Spider-Man's popularity with younger children, this prompted much controversy. The BBFC defended their decision, arguing that the film could have been given a '15'. Despite this, North Norfolk and Breckland District Councils, in East Anglia, changed it to a 'PG', and Tameside council,
      <a href="/wiki/Manchester" title="Manchester">
       Manchester
      </a>
      , denoted it a 'PG-12'. The U.S. rated it "PG-13"
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43">
       <a href="#cite_note-43">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        43
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      for "stylized violence and action". In late August, the BBFC relaxed their policy to '12A', leading Sony to re-release the film.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44">
       <a href="#cite_note-44">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        44
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Reception">
       Reception
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Spider-Man_(2002_film)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Reception">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Box_office_performance">
       Box office performance
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Spider-Man_(2002_film)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Box office performance">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      <i>
       Spider-Man
      </i>
      was a major commercial success, becoming the first film to pass the $100 million mark in a single weekend. With the release in the United States and Canada on May 3, 2002 on 7,500 screens at 3,615 theaters, the film earned $39,406,872 on its opening day, averaging $10,901 per theater ($5,524.25 per screen). This was the highest-opening day at the time until it was surpassed by its sequel,
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Spider-Man_2" title="Spider-Man 2">
        Spider-Man 2
       </a>
      </i>
      , in 2004.
      <i>
       Spider-Man
      </i>
      also set an all-time record for the highest earnings in a single day with $43,622,264 on May 4, 2002, a record later surpassed by
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Shrek_2" title="Shrek 2">
        Shrek 2
       </a>
      </i>
      in 2004. The film earned a total of $114,844,116 during its opening weekend, averaging $31,769 per theater ($15,312.55 per screen) and became the fastest theatrical release to reach $100 million at the time, crossing the milestone in three days.
      <i>
       Spider-Man
      </i>
      also had the highest-opening week in North America box office film for a non-sequel, with $114 million, which was surpassed eight years later by
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Alice_in_Wonderland_(2010_film)" title="Alice in Wonderland (2010 film)">
        Alice in Wonderland
       </a>
      </i>
      in 2010.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45">
       <a href="#cite_note-45">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        45
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The film's three-day record was later surpassed by
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Pirates_of_the_Caribbean:_Dead_Man%27s_Chest" title="Pirates of the Caribbean: Dead Man's Chest">
        Pirates of the Caribbean: Dead Man's Chest
       </a>
      </i>
      in 2006.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46">
       <a href="#cite_note-46">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        46
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The film stayed at the top position in its second weekend, dropping only 38% in its second weekend, grossing another $71,417,527, averaging $19,755.89 per theater ($9,522.34 per screen) and bringing the ten-day total to $223,040,031. The film dropped to the second position in its third weekend, behind
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Star_Wars_Episode_II:_Attack_of_the_Clones" title="Star Wars Episode II: Attack of the Clones">
        Star Wars Episode II: Attack of the Clones
       </a>
      </i>
      , but still made $45,036,912, dropping only 37%, averaging $12,458 per theater, and bringing the seventeen-day tally to $285,573,668. It stayed at the second position in its fourth weekend, grossing $35,814,844 over the four-day Memorial Day frame, dropping only 21% while expanding to 3,876 theaters, averaging $9,240 over four days, and bringing the twenty-five day gross to $333,641,492.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47">
       <a href="#cite_note-47">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        47
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      In the box office,
      <i>
       Spider-Man
      </i>
      became 2002's highest-grossing film with $403,706,375 in the U.S. and Canada, defeating
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/The_Lord_of_the_Rings:_The_Two_Towers" title="The Lord of the Rings: The Two Towers">
        The Lord of the Rings: The Two Towers
       </a>
      </i>
      and
      <i>
       Star Wars Episode II: Attack of the Clones
      </i>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48">
       <a href="#cite_note-48">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        48
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <i>
       Spider-Man
      </i>
      currently ranks as the
      <a href="/wiki/List_of_highest-grossing_films_in_Canada_and_the_United_States" title="List of highest-grossing films in Canada and the United States">
       fifteenth highest-grossing film of all time
      </a>
      in the U.S. and Canada. The film also grossed $821,708,551 worldwide, making it 2002's third highest-grossing film behind
      <i>
       The Lord of the Rings: The Two Towers
      </i>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Harry_Potter_and_the_Chamber_of_Secrets_(film)" title="Harry Potter and the Chamber of Secrets (film)">
       <i>
        Harry Potter and the Chamber of Secrets
       </i>
      </a>
      , and the
      <a href="/wiki/List_of_highest-grossing_films" title="List of highest-grossing films">
       42nd highest-grossing film of all time
      </a>
      .
     </p>
     <p>
      International markets which generated grosses in excess of $10 million include Australia ($16.9 million), Brazil ($17.4 million), France, Algeria, Monaco, Morocco and Tunisia ($32.9 million), Germany ($30.7 million), Italy ($20.8 million), Japan ($56.2 million), Mexico ($31.2 million), South Korea ($16.98 million), Spain ($23.7 million), and the United Kingdom, Ireland and Malta ($45.8 million).
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BOMINT_49-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-BOMINT-49">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        49
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      <i>
       Spider-Man
      </i>
      became the highest-grossing superhero film of all time at the time of its release. It was eventually outgrossed in 2007 by
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Spider-Man_3" title="Spider-Man 3">
        Spider-Man 3
       </a>
      </i>
      . In 2008,
      <i>
       Spider-Man 3
      </i>
      was outgrossed by
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/The_Dark_Knight_(film)" title="The Dark Knight (film)">
        The Dark Knight
       </a>
      </i>
      . In 2012,
      <i>
       The Dark Knight
      </i>
      was outgrossed by
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/The_Avengers_(2012_film)" title="The Avengers (2012 film)">
        The Avengers
       </a>
      </i>
      .
      <i>
       Spider-Man
      </i>
      currently ranks as the sixth highest-grossing superhero film of all time.
     </p>
     <p>
      The film's U.S. television rights (
      <a href="/wiki/Fox_Broadcasting_Company" title="Fox Broadcasting Company">
       Fox
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/TBS_(TV_channel)" title="TBS (TV channel)">
       TBS
      </a>
      /
      <a href="/wiki/TNT_(TV_channel)" title="TNT (TV channel)">
       TNT
      </a>
      ) were sold for $60 million.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-the-numbers.com_50-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-the-numbers.com-50">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        50
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Related gross toy sales were $109 million.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-the-numbers.com_50-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-the-numbers.com-50">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        50
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Its U.S. DVD revenue as of July 2004 stands at $338.8 million.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-the-numbers.com_50-2">
       <a href="#cite_note-the-numbers.com-50">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        50
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Its U.S. VHS revenue as of July 2004 is $89.2 million.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-the-numbers.com_50-3">
       <a href="#cite_note-the-numbers.com-50">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        50
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Critical_response">
       Critical response
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Spider-Man_(2002_film)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Critical response">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      <i>
       Spider-Man
      </i>
      received critical acclaim. Review aggregator website
      <a href="/wiki/Rotten_Tomatoes" title="Rotten Tomatoes">
       Rotten Tomatoes
      </a>
      calculated an 89% overall approval based on 216 reviews.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51">
       <a href="#cite_note-51">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        51
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The casting, mainly Tobey Maguire, is often cited as one of the film's high points. Eric Harrison, of the
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Houston_Chronicle" title="Houston Chronicle">
        Houston Chronicle
       </a>
      </i>
      , was initially skeptical of the casting of Tobey Maguire, but, after seeing the film, he stated, "within seconds, however, it becomes hard to imagine anyone else in the role."
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Harrison_52-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Harrison-52">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        52
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/USA_Today" title="USA Today">
        USA Today
       </a>
      </i>
      critic Mike Clark believed the casting rivaled that of
      <a href="/wiki/Christopher_Reeve" title="Christopher Reeve">
       Christopher Reeve
      </a>
      as 1978's
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Superman_(1978_film)" title="Superman (1978 film)">
        Superman
       </a>
      </i>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Mike_Clark_53-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Mike_Clark-53">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        53
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Owen Gleiberman, of
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Entertainment_Weekly" title="Entertainment Weekly">
        Entertainment Weekly
       </a>
      </i>
      , had mixed feelings about the casting, particularly Tobey Maguire. "Maguire, winning as he is, never quite gets the chance to bring the two sides of Spidey — the boy and the man, the romantic and the avenger — together."
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gleiberman_54-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Gleiberman-54">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        54
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/The_Hollywood_Reporter" title="The Hollywood Reporter">
        The Hollywood Reporter
       </a>
       '
      </i>
      s Kirk Honeycutt thought, "the filmmakers' imaginations work in overdrive from the clever design of the cobwebby opening credits and Spider-Man and M.J.'s upside down kiss — after one of his many rescues of her — to a finale that leaves character relationships open ended for future adventures."
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hollywood_Reporter_55-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Hollywood_Reporter-55">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        55
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Conversely,
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/LA_Weekly" title="LA Weekly">
        LA Weekly
       </a>
       '
      </i>
      s
      <a href="/wiki/Manohla_Dargis" title="Manohla Dargis">
       Manohla Dargis
      </a>
      wrote, "It isn't that Spider-Man is inherently unsuited for live-action translation; it's just that he's not particularly interesting or, well, animated."
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56">
       <a href="#cite_note-56">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        56
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Giving it 2.5/4 stars,
      <a href="/wiki/Roger_Ebert" title="Roger Ebert">
       Roger Ebert
      </a>
      felt the film lacked a decent action element; "Consider the scene where Spider-Man is given a cruel choice between saving Mary Jane or a cable car full of school kids. He tries to save both, so that everyone dangles from webbing that seems about to pull loose. The visuals here could have given an impression of the enormous weights and tensions involved, but instead the scene seems more like a bloodless storyboard of the idea."
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ebert_57-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Ebert-57">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        57
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Stylistically, there was heavy criticism of the
      <a href="/wiki/Green_Goblin" title="Green Goblin">
       Green Goblin
      </a>
      's costume, which led IGN's Richard George to comment years later, "We're not saying the comic book costume is exactly thrilling, but the Goblin armor (the helmet in particular) from
      <i>
       Spider-Man
      </i>
      is almost comically bad... Not only is it not frightening, it prohibits expression."
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58">
       <a href="#cite_note-58">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        58
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Entertainment_Weekly" title="Entertainment Weekly">
        Entertainment Weekly
       </a>
      </i>
      put "the kiss in
      <i>
       Spider-Man
      </i>
      " on its end-of-the-decade "best-of" list, saying, "There's a fine line between romantic and corny. And the rain-soaked smooch between Spider-Man and Mary Jane from 2002 tap-dances right on that line. The reason it works? Even if she suspects he's Peter Parker, she doesn't try to find out. And that's sexy."
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59">
       <a href="#cite_note-59">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        59
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <i>
       Empire
      </i>
      magazine ranked
      <i>
       Spider-Man
      </i>
      437 in its
      <i>
       500 Greatest Movies of All Time
      </i>
      list the following year.
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Awards">
       Awards
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Spider-Man_(2002_film)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Awards">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article:
      <a href="/wiki/List_of_accolades_received_by_the_Spider-Man_film_series" title="List of accolades received by the Spider-Man film series">
       List of accolades received by the Spider-Man film series
      </a>
     </div>
     <p>
      The film won several awards ranging from
      <a href="/wiki/Teen_Choice_Awards" title="Teen Choice Awards">
       Teen Choice Awards
      </a>
      to the
      <a href="/wiki/Saturn_Award" title="Saturn Award">
       Saturn Awards
      </a>
      , and was also nominated for two
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Academy_Award" title="Academy Award">
       Academy Awards
      </a>
      ("
      <a href="/wiki/Academy_Award_for_Best_Visual_Effects" title="Academy Award for Best Visual Effects">
       Best Visual Effects
      </a>
      " and "
      <a href="/wiki/Academy_Award_for_Best_Sound" title="Academy Award for Best Sound">
       Best Sound Mixing
      </a>
      " (
      <a href="/wiki/Kevin_O%27Connell_(sound_re-recording_mixer)" title="Kevin O'Connell (sound re-recording mixer)">
       Kevin O'Connell
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Greg_P._Russell" title="Greg P. Russell">
       Greg P. Russell
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Ed_Novick" title="Ed Novick">
       Ed Novick
      </a>
      )), but lost to
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/The_Lord_of_the_Rings:_The_Two_Towers" title="The Lord of the Rings: The Two Towers">
        The Lord of the Rings: The Two Towers
       </a>
      </i>
      and
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Chicago_(2002_film)" title="Chicago (2002 film)">
        Chicago
       </a>
      </i>
      , respectively.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Oscars2003_60-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Oscars2003-60">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        60
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Awards_61-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Awards-61">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        61
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      While only Danny Elfman brought home a Saturn Award, Raimi, Maguire, and Dunst were all nominated for their respective positions. It also took home the
      <a href="/wiki/People%27s_Choice_Awards" title="People's Choice Awards">
       People's Choice Award
      </a>
      for "Favorite Motion Picture."
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Awards_61-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-Awards-61">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        61
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The film was nominated for Favorite Movie at the
      <a href="/wiki/Nickelodeon_Kids%27_Choice_Awards" title="Nickelodeon Kids' Choice Awards">
       Nickelodeon Kids' Choice Awards
      </a>
      , but lost to
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Austin_Powers_in_Goldmember" title="Austin Powers in Goldmember">
        Austin Powers in Goldmember
       </a>
      </i>
      .
     </p>

         </a>

         <a href="/wiki/Willem_Dafoe" title="Willem Dafoe">

         </a>
        </td>

        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <td>
         <a href="/wiki/People%27s_Choice_Awards" title="People's Choice Awards">
          People's Choice Awards
         </a>
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70">
          <a href="#cite_note-70">
           <span>
            [
           </span>
           70
           <span>
            ]
           </span>
          </a>
         </sup>
        </td>
        <td>
         January 12, 2003

     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Sequel">
       Sequel
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Spider-Man_(2002_film)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Sequel">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article:
      <a href="/wiki/Spider-Man_2" title="Spider-Man 2">
       Spider-Man 2
      </a>
     </div>
     <p>
      On January 2003, Sony revealed that a sequel to
      <i>
       Spider-Man
      </i>
      was in development, and was produced and directed by
      <a href="/wiki/Sam_Raimi" title="Sam Raimi">
       Sam Raimi
      </a>
      . On 15 March 2003, a trailer revealed that the film will be released in 2004. In 2007, a sequel to both Spider-Man 2 and Spider-Man was announced, apparently with the "entirely" new cast and characters. This sequel is called
      <i>
       Spider-Man 3
      </i>
      , and it was released in 4 May 2007.
     </p>

         </span>
         <span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ASpider-Man+%282002+film%29&amp;rft.btitle=2003+Taurus+World+Stunt+Awards+Nominations&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.taurusworldstuntawards.com%2Ffileadmin%2Fcontent%2Fshow%2F2003__Nominees_and_Winners.pdf&amp;rft.pub=World+Stunt+Awards&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook">
          <span style="display:none;">
          </span>
         </span>
        </span>
       </li>
